I was generally pleased with the 305 but wanted something a little more sleek and less bulky and to that end the 405 meets expectations.  I was also able to obtain a satellite signal more rapidly with the 405.  But that's all there is in terms of upside.<br /><br />In exchange for those minor advantages you have to deal with the flawed design of the &#34;bezel&#34;.  It is an absolute nightmare to use while exercising since the moisture from perspiration interferes with it.  I use the device primarily for running, cycling and mountain biking.  Many times I use a heart rate monitor that - on a positive note - pairs very well with the Forerunner.  However, in order to switch screens to see your heart rate or review any data you need to use the bezel.  I don't believe I perspire any more than average (in fact I bet less than the average guy) but any moisture whatsoever interferes with the bezel.  It is extremely frustrating.  For those of you that run with the iPod Nano and try to change songs once you've started sweating it is a very similar issue.  I have tried running with a towel to try to keep my one hand dry but it provided only a slight improvement.<br /><br />What struck me was that I was allowing a device that is supposed to assist me in exercising actually negatively affect my workouts.  Instead of considering another GPS watch device I have since changed my philosophy.  I now run with my smartphone and use one of the GPS apps I've downloaded.  The best ones in my opinion are Cyclemeter and SportsTracker.  They provide comparable data that you get from Garmin's website (in fact what you get on your phone is more than what Garmin shows on the device itself.)  I never have to worry about taking my device as I always have my phone with me.  Since the app is intergrated into the phone I get all the updates, i.e. speed, pace distance, through my earbuds with no need tolook at my phone.  And I believe both are either free or cost $2 or $3 to download.  The added bonus is that I no longer use the iPod Nano as my iPhone has all the music I need.  In short, ditch the watch and use your smartphone.  It's better, easier and significantly CHEAPER!

B0098WWEH8|5.0|\\"Shields\\", Grizzly Bear's fourth and latest full-length album, falls somewhere between \\"Yellow House\\" and \\"Veckatimest\\", not in likability, but, rather, in construction, which may make it their most accomplished effort to date. In my first spin of \\"Shields\\" nothing struck me with the immediacy of \\"Two Weeks\\" or \\"While I Wait for the Others\\", nothing as dazzling as \\"Cheerleaders\\" or \\"Foreground\\". Veckatimest, metaphorically, was like receiving fellatio from someone you've always lusted after but who you've perceived as lacking the character to actually fall in love with, that is until that moment when you are gifted with the glorious sensations of their love. Afterwards asleep in one another's arms, you wonder all night who this beautiful maniac is anyways, to make you feel so enamored suddenly and where it was they came from. \\"Shields\\" isn't the type of record that will give you that kind of instant gratification again but it will give you an idea of who the bewitching creature you have fallen in love with is really. In contrast, \\"Yellow House\\", which I purchased after viewing a late night television rendition of \\"On a Neck, On a Spit\\", produced a response that would take time to catch up with. Initially I was disappointed with the entirety of \\"Yellow House\\" because I had anticipated more of a guitar and drum type record as opposed to the minimalist instrumentation and concentrated vocal harmonies that played so fundamental to its complexity. I would not appreciate its arrangements until a year later when I stumbled upon the song \\"Knife\\" by accident, faintly recognizing it, connecting with it, falling under a spell of sorts, pulling the album from it's dusty shelf because of this chance encounter and reexamining it with slightly more weathered eyes. In my reintroduction I was overwhelmed by what I could not see before, maybe because I was not in the same place I had been a year previous in life. Sometimes you have to be in the right place at the right time to identify with and appreciate certain music, books or films. This factor, in a much diluted sense, came into play upon repeated listens to \\"Shields\\" in which tracks such as \\"Sleeping Ute\\", \\"Yet Again\\", \\"A Simple Answer\\" and \\"Sun in your Eyes\\" began to stand out with specific shape, colors, emotions and intents, as marvelously textured songs do, becoming more fulfilling as one grows to know the depth of their circles. \\"Shields\\" is the mastery of everything the band has learned through their previous efforts coalesced with a sense of identity, realized in a balance of both accessibility and challenge that lend to the possibility that \\"Shields\\" may be as timeless, if not more so, than both its predecessors. As for the year at hand it certainly is one of the most rewarding listens out there.

B005N7CA3A|5.0|While most might say that this piece of work is considerably different from his past two works, Secret Codes and Battleships is one of his finest works to be put out on the market. After the success of Spin and the acclaim of The Tension and The Spark, Darren Hayes went personally into This Delicate Thing We've Made, exploring all aspects of synth music and keyboard sounds. To incorporate an orchestra while maintaining the same pop sound from the old days of other works would be slightly difficult for those not strong in the business or young. Darren Hayes exquisitely performs this enough to be acclaimed. The lyricism is still natural of Hayes, romantic affections and the like, but still a reminder of days gone by when lyricism was the most important part of songwriting. The entire album feels like a river, never choppy or out of place; everything sticks together. Of course, there are standouts: \\"Bloodstained Heart\\" is one of the best of his career (even with Savage Garden), and \\"Taken By the Sea\\" is a wonderful start song to the album. B008G12ERC|3.0|First off, you see my star rating for this album? 3 stars? That means I think the album has good points, and -dramatic music- bad points too.If you down thumb my review, please state why, as I'm not someone who gives everything in near sight a 4 or 5 star rating. The purpose of a review is to state your opinion and not to act all fanboyish over the product at hand. You're not going to change my opinion, and I wouldnt dream of changing yours. But if in the comments, you have some insightful comments to offer, like \\"listen to this track again, there's a lot you might have missed\\", I might just consider it.<br /><br />I'll admit, I'm in ways, a latecomer to the Muse party. I didn't get into them until 2009. I heard all their albums before the Resistance and loved them all. Resistance is not a bad album, it's a decent one and despite a few cringe worthy tunes, there were still some good ones. When I heard the derpstep in the trailer for this album, I was a tad worried. Is their new album really a pile of dubstep crap? Are they jumping on the bandwagon, when they're such a ridiculously talented band? Nonetheless, after hearing the Olympics song, which I really disliked, and Madness, which was a nice tune, and Unsustainable, which is a nice mix of genres and the dubstep track, I figured I'd give it a listen.<br /><br />And so it's at this point where I'm guessing you're expecting a justification of my rating for the album. If you took away the two dubstep-tinged tracks, you have just another Muse album. Which is exactly the problem- Muse have played it too safely with this album and decided to just take the classic Muse approach. While it isn't bad, it leaves me thinking that band are so much more talented than this, and that they could write, and innovate in different ways if they wanted to. Notice how different \\"Origin of Symmetry\\" is from \\"Showbiz\\"? And \\"The Resistance\\" from \\"Black Holes\\"? Yet all of them have the \\"Muse\\" sound, that remains consistent through the band's albums. Problem is, the band didn't change much from The Resistance. They just figured \\"that album sold, and we could record ourselves taking a shower and folks will eat it up\\", so they just went with... Muse, as a sound for the album. Even if Chris states that \\"We tried something radically different\\", he's wrong, it's just another Muse album.<br /><br />\\"Supremacy\\" starts off the album, and it's a decent tune. Has a bit of a 007 feel to it, like it wouldn't be out of place in the new James Bond movie, \\"Skyfall\\". The verses are cool and I love the big drums as well as the marching drum beat throughout. The strings are probably the first thing you notice about the tune, and while they don't totally intrude, sadly the song could have survived without them. \\"Madness\\" is next. The song has the underlying motif of a beat built around Matt softly singing \\"M-m-m-m-m-m-m-m-mad-mad-mad\\", which obviously amounts to him completing the word \\"madness\\" at the end. The song's lyrics were written after Bellamy got in a fight with his girlfriend Kate Hudson, and are nice and heartfelt. Towards the end, the song starts to take a bit of a U2 direction, as it wouldn't sound out of place on the \\"Zooropa\\" album.<br /><br />Next is \\"Panic Station\\", a song that sounds a bit like a mix of a Franz Ferdinand tune and \\"Supermassive Black Hole\\". It's catchy and all, but it just isn't what Muse is known for. I don't hate it like everyone else does,  but I'd willingly skip it, and the next track, \\"Prelude\\", which isn't really important at all.<br /><br />Sadly, Muse will never live down the next track, \\"Survival\\". It was written for the Olympics, and hell, even that annoying \\"I Believe\\" song by Nikki Yanofsky (the song of the Vancouver 2010 winter Olympics) feels more Olympics than this. The opening of the tune is cringe worthy, but thankfully when the singing kicks in, it starts to get tolerable, until the choir from The Omen soundtrack start chanting \\"So I told you\\" and \\"You were warned and didn't listen\\" for absolutely no reason at all. The song is easy the most over-the-top thing I've ever heard in my life, and not in a good way. If you want to write a song for the Olympics, why not just do a typical Muse track like \\"Time is Running Out\\" or \\"Resistance\\", instead of wasting a perfectly talented choir and making it sound like Queen singing a theme for a Tim Burton movie?<br /><br />Thankfully things pick up afterword, with the next track being \\"Follow Me\\". It starts with the sound of a baby's heart beat, and Matt crooning a lovely tune. The song starts to sound a bit like \\"MK Ultra\\" from their previous albums before the dubstep beat kicks in, and even then it's tolerable. It's a fun track that at the same time sounds really much like a filler track. \\"Animals\\" might be my favourite song in the album- a soft, subdued rocker that wouldn't be out of place on Origin of Symmetry, and reminds me a bit of a more uptempo \\"Screenager\\". The song closes with a rather frightening sound clip from the Wall Street Trading Floor, which explains the song's meaning- it's about the greed of people in the stock market, and how they show no regard for others, only caring about themselves. Sadly, it's followed by \\"Explorers\\", a song so forgettable I can't even remember anything about it.<br /><br />Big Freeze is a catchy tune, but THOSE LYRICS. While listening to it, I thought to myself, \\"if I hear the words Don't give up' one more time, I'm throwing this CD in the garbage\\", as I heard them several times throughout (and similar phrases too). It's a shame, because the song's music is fine enough. \\"Save Me\\" and \\"Liquid State\\" are most known for having Christopher Wolstenholme singing. As he's my favourite member of the band, I was anticipating these tracks greatly. And he's a decent singer, he sounds a bit like the guy from Finger Eleven. But there's a reason he doesn't sing for Muse. \\"Liquid State\\" is the better of these two tracks, mainly because it's faster and heavier, but both tracks are really forgettable and the album would have survived without them.<br /><br />The last two tracks are the finale of the album, and both are very different. Starting off with \\"The 2nd Law: Unsustainable\\". People accuse this song of being too much of an attempt to jump on the brostep bandwagon, but I think it's a very intriguing mix of genres. It starts off as a classical tune that wouldn't be out of place in a Zack Snyder film. There's an interesting monologue explaining the 2nd law of therodynamics. \\"New energy cannot be created and if high energy  is being destroyed, an economy based on endless growth is...\\" is suddenly cut off by a robot voice phonetically saying \\"UN...SUSTAINABLE\\", before the song explodes into a brostep breakdown. And despite my utter distaste of dubstep, the breakdown sounds awesome. For starters, the band actually plays the dubstep part on their instruments, as opposed to Skrillex and (insert generic step musician here), who does it all on a computer. Then a few bars of proggy symphonic rock pla, with Matt vocalizing, which manages to be very epic feeling. Then, after another monologue and epic drumming, the brostep part comes back in again.<br /><br />Next is \\"Isolated System\\". There's no dubstep here, and the song is more trance influenced than anything. The song loops the line from the previous song, \\"In an isolated system, the entropy can only increase. The song is decidedly more trance influenced, and has a subdued. electro-trance beat  throughout. This is a truly unique track. It feels very subdued, and also like there's a lot of rage and energy dying to get out at the same time.<br /><br />The 2nd Law is very different from its predecessor. They're similar in the sense that they're both complete messes. But The Resistance is a mess that somehow manages to keep moving in a straight line, has a sense of direction and knows where it's headed. The 2nd Law is more like a six year old kid with ADHD telling a story. It constantly loses track of where it's going, and seems to not know what its goal really is. The album feels more like a compilation instead of an album- the tracks feel really out of sequence and like the band didn't seem to know what they wanted with the album.<br /><br /> Problem is, it's too much of a Muse album, even for a Muse album. I really would like if they decided to do something outside their comfort zone. And it's not like they have to radically change, I mean, hell, my favourite band, Iron Maiden change all the time and yet still have that Iron Maiden sound. But they don't make it so that they just get lazy and take the classic Route.<br /><br />Yet, the album is still very listenable and there's a good number of standout tracks. Sure it's my 2nd least favourite of their albums (The Resistance takes that top spot), but it's enjoyable to an extent, and I'd like to hear how the tracks sound live.both tracks are really forgettable and the album would have survived without them.<br /><br />The last two tracks are the finale of the album, and both are very different. Starting off with \\"The 2nd Law: Unsustainable\\". People accuse this song of being too much of an attempt to jump on the brostep bandwagon, but I think it's a very intriguing mix of genres. It starts off as a classical tune that wouldn't be out of place in a Zack Snyder film. There's an interesting monologue explaining the 2nd law of therodynamics. \\"New energy cannot be created and if high energy  is being destroyed, an economy based on endless growth is...\\" is suddenly cut off by a robot voice phonetically saying \\"UN...SUSTAINABLE\\", before the song explodes into a brostep breakdown. And despite my utter distaste of dubstep, the breakdown sounds awesome. For starters, the band actually plays the dubstep part on their instruments, as opposed to Skrillex and (insert generic step musician here), who does it all on a computer. Then a few bars of proggy symphonic rock pla, with Matt vocalizing, which manages to be very epic feeling. Then, after another monologue and epic drumming, the brostep part comes back in again.<br /><br />Next is \\"Isolated System\\". There's no dubstep here, and the song is more trance influenced than anything. The song loops the line from the previous song, \\"In an isolated system, the entropy can only increase. The song is decidedly more trance influenced, and has a subdued. electro-trance beat  throughout. This is a truly unique track. It feels very subdued, and also like there's a lot of rage and energy dying to get out at the same time.<br /><br />The 2nd Law is very different from its predecessor. They're similar in the sense that they're both complete messes. But The Resistance is a mess that somehow manages to keep moving in a straight line, has a sense of direction and knows where it's headed. The 2nd Law is more like a six year old kid with ADHD telling a story. It constantly loses track of where it's going, and seems to not know what its goal really is. The album feels more like a compilation instead of an album- the tracks feel really out of sequence and like the band didn't seem to know what they wanted with the album.<br /><br /> Problem is, it's too much of a Muse album, even for a Muse album. I really would like if they decided to do something outside their comfort zone. And it's not like they have to radically change, I mean, hell, my favourite band, Iron Maiden change all the time and yet still have that Iron Maiden sound. But they don't make it so that they just get lazy and take the classic Route.<br /><br />Yet, the album is still very listenable and there's a good number of standout tracks. Sure it's my 2nd least favourite of their albums (The Resistance takes that top spot), but it's enjoyable to an extent, and I'd like to hear how the tracks sound live.

B008673ZAQ|3.0|Okay, so Sylvia Day blew me away with Bared to You, and Reflected was one of my most-anticipated releases for the fall.  I couldn't wait to dive back into Gideon and Eva's intense relationship to see how they were going to get past all of the (MANY) skeletons in their closets.  While it wasn't the mind-blowing whirlwind of steaming hot torment I was hoping it would be, this was an okay read that I hope is a lead-in to some big things for the third book.<br /><br />Reflected primarily concentrates on four basic principles:<br /><br />-Gideon and Eva having LOTS of sex (and WOW...It. Was. HOT!)<br />-Gideon hiding his feelings and being an overbearing jerk, while not concerning himself with how it affects Eva<br />-Heart-wrenching bouts of justified jealousy and the resulting crushing blow on Eva's emotions<br />-A few tender moments thrown in between, along with some pointless therapy<br /><br />I'm not breaking it down like that to be negative, but this is just essentially what happens repeatedly all throughout the story, up until the very end when we finally get some answers and realize (at least partially) why Gideon was being such an ass. So here's my issue; I LOVED the steamy scenes. Day really outdid herself this time around with several moments that had my pulse skyrocketting (that post-concert limo scene...YUMMERS)!!!  But at some point, there needed to be something behind all of the great, intense, mind-numbing sex.  I mean, even Day recognizes this point in the story, she has them talk about how their relationship needs to be more than just sex!!!  It was this never-ending cycle of no real substance, and it was just so monotonous. What I was hoping for and entirely expected was some real development in their relationship; sweet dates out on the town, moments where they kick back and enjoy something fun together, nights at home snuggling while they talked about something...ANYTHING. Take for example the adorable, sexy email banter that we all loved so much between Ana and Christian in Fifty Shades. Even something that trivial added into the story made them seem like a real couple that could simply enjoy each other, even with all the mess in their lives.  We don't get any of that here, and it really made their relationship feel lacking, much to Eva's agreement.<br /><br />I wanted so badly for Eva to walk away...REALLY walk away, so that Gideon would finally get it.  I don't know what happened to the Gideon I fell so hard for in Bared, because he wasn't here in this book until the very end.  The cocky, sexy alpha-male went all coldhearted angry dom on us, and I really missed the sweet seduction that made me melt in Bared.  There's one really dramatic twist that seems to make him fully understand, followed by an emotion-filled section of the story that I loved.  But then Gideon does a complete 180 all over again!  As much as I wanted Eva to get a backbone, I couldn't help but feel sorry for her after the yo-yo act  Gideon put her through. I wanted him to experience gut-wrenching emotional pain for what she had to feel!  We do eventually discover what was behind his final \\"assholery\\", but at that point it was just too much.  That section of the book would have been the perfect heart-crushing torment that I love in a great romance, if it weren't for the multiple boomerang moments prior.<br /><br />I'm really not trying to bash this book; I'm giving it 3 out of 5 stars because I did enjoy it more than I disliked it. I was virtual high-fiving Eva a few times when she told Gideon where he could shove it, and I was very happy that it drove him mad!!  And of course the chemistry between Gideon and Eva is clearly off-the-charts, and I love the intensity of it.  Some of the dramatic twists were great; the addition of Eva's ex Brett and his determination to win her over  really put some excitement into the storyline, and like I said, I really loved the heartbreaking lead into the ending.  I am such a sucker for stories that have that intense jealousy and world-crushing heartbreak, and Day wrote it to perfection here.  I remain hopeful that with the next book we will finally get to the core of Gideon's past so he can let go and truly love Eva, because this series started out too good to end up a disappointment.

B0084IG8TM|5.0|I've reviewed the insanely popular book The Hunger Games in both written and video form. The video review still continues to be one of the most viewed on YouTube and is one of my most viewed videos. That just says something about how a story can have so much of an impact. The film version of the first book of the series was sure to be a success with an already astounding fan base, so I was quite eager to check it out. Luckily, I was able to get press access to an early screening of this one (yay me!), which made it all the more exciting.<br /><br />The film is directed by Gary Ross, which was a surprising choice for me. He's most known for films like Seabiscuit and Pleasantville, so I was unsure how he'd handle such an over-the-top production that the material called for. He ended up being a fine choice however, as the book's fantastical futuristic and post-apocalyptic world was translated perfectly onto the screen. The writing is also done by Ross, with the book's author Suzanne Collins and Billy Ray contributing to the screenplay. The follows very closely to the book, which was certainly a wise choice in order to not upset the already huge group of book fans that were guaranteed to purchase a ticket.<br /><br />The Hunger Games follows 12 districts which formerly made up North America, now known as Panem. Panem is run by a totalitarian government known as the Capitol. Each year the Capitol reminds the citizens of their control by holding the Hunger Games, a fight-to-the-death survival competition featuring a boy and girl chosen at random from each district. The concept may sound similar, as the idea has been done in many other books and movies, however The Hunger Games still does manage to be unique enough to hold its own. There have been constant comparisons to other certain titles, however I find such comparisons pointless as the characters and world Collins created are original and interesting.<br /><br />The story centers on 16 year old Katniss Everdeen (Jennifer Lawrence) of the rustic and impoverished District 12. During the Reaping, or selection ceremony for the tributes that will represent the district in the games, Katniss' younger sister Prim (Willow Shields) gets chosen. Without a second thought, Katniss throws herself forward and volunteers to take Prim's place. The boy chosen is Peeta Mellark (Josh Hutcherson), and shortly after the two head towards the Capitol for their training where they are introduced to a world unlike anything they have seen in their village.<br /><br />The Capitol was where most of my worries about the film adaptation existed. The futuristic world called for technology that doesn't exist and wild clothing and hairdos (and skindos), which I wasn't sure if they'd be able to match my imagination's interpretation. However I was pleasantly surprised at the film's ability to capture the book's descriptions nearly perfectly. Not that I deny the ability of the talented individuals that have churned out some breathtaking effects and designs over the past several years, but it's tough I think for a film to match what most people picture when reading the book. In this case, I think they nailed it.<br /><br />Once the games actually kick off, the excitement doesn't let up. For fans of survival adventure movies such as myself, the film is a treat. There's an excellent display of survival techniques and tactical scenarios. While the film does don a PG-13 rating, there is also a surprising amount of violence involved. The story, after all, does involve kids killing kids, but the film is impressively able to pull of some of the more gruesome scenes without exploiting the gore and carnage. The action scenes are adrenaline-filled, which is good but could also give some viewers motion sickness. The camera work is fast, moving right along at the pace of the action. I liked the style at times, but the shaky cam also did hinder the detail of some of the combat scenes.<br /><br />The pacing of the film also works both in favor of and against the movie. At over 2 hours long, it feels much shorter. Because of this, however, many scenes that in the book were very emotional and significant seemed very much rushed past in the film, placing more attention to the action. I understand there's a lot of ground to cover with the story, and in order to keep it to one part they had to do a bit of cramming, but a few pivotal scenes were either ignored or barely touched on which was a disappointment.<br /><br />Being highly impressed with Lawrence in Winter's Bone, I knew she would tackle the role of Katniss with ease and she certainly did. I'm not usually too impressed with Josh Hutcherson, but I felt he did well as Peeta. The rest of the cast was just perfect, from Woody Harrelson as the drunken mentor Haymitch, to the always impressive Stanley Tucci as Caesar Flickerman. The colorful characters were represented well, and I felt like the actors really brought each one to life.<br /><br />The film overall is a great example of a book adaptation done well. There may have been a few things I would have liked to have seen, but it captures a huge amount of detail in a relatively short time that seems to go by without notice. With the Games' impressive arena, full of manipulated nature and engineered animals, combined with a perfect cast and action that never lets up once it gets started, I can imagine without having read the book there really wouldn't be a lot to be unimpressed with. While the books may be popular with the female teen audience, due to its empowering heroine, this is a matured teen survival adventure flick that adults of both sexes can enjoy.<br />Source: criticnic.com 28-July-2012s both in favor of and against the movie. At over 2 hours long, it feels much shorter. B003XF1XOQ|3.0|Clearly, the author is trying to convey a message in the book - 'war is bad; everybody loses.' She has used quite a few tools in doing so - killing off our favorite characters, showing the emotional trauma that the characters experience, stories of war crimes and how war causes otherwise good people to do bad things, etc. There is no problem with all of this if the author does this elegantly. Instead, in this book, she tries to cram far too much story into too few pages. This may make for a 'good' (or mediocre) generic action movie, but not a good book. Maybe she is trying to show that everything happens quickly in war and lots can happen in little time, but it just kills the quality of the story. Then there is also the question of whether the characters' actions are believable. While I am no psychologist and am not able to judge whether the characters would actually act this way under those circumstances, all of it seems just too absurd and convenient (to convey the author's point) such that it decreases the entertainment value of the story. Finally, there is also the issue of the author introducing all these events into the story that conveniently conveys the horror and atrocities of war regardless of how they blend into the overall story.<br /><br />In summary, imagine that you are given a writing assignment where you have to write a story that continues from a prior work. You have certain requirements such as page length and a list of horrors of war that you must describe.  Your final product is a book titled 'Mockingjay'.

Nothing however is how it seems this film which has some fascinating twists and turns but is, ultimately, absurd. First thing that we need to get out of the way is the fact that &#34;The Tall Man&#34; despite the advertising and the first 40 or so minutes is NOT a horror film nor is it really a supernatural film. If you temper your expectations with this in mind you might enjoy the film but, more than likely, you'll find &#34;The Tall Man&#34; a mildly interesting failure.<br /><br />SPOILERS:<br /><br />Julia Benning (Jessica Biel) serves as a nurse in the dying mining town of Cold Rock unfortunately the town is best known now as a town where most of its children go missing. Local legend suggests that the children are being taken by a mysterious entity nicknamed The Tall Man. When David is taken Benning desperately pursues the attacker to retrieve the child.<br /><br />MAJOR SPOILER:<br /><br />As the story progresses we discover that Julia has been abducting the children feeding them to a secret network headed by her husband who places these kidnapped children from impoverished backgrounds to &#34;deserving&#34; families (largely upper and middle class from what we can tell in the movie). When the town's people find out she refuses to divulge what, exactly, happened to the children suggesting that she killed them to protect the children and their new families.<br /><br />END OF SPOILERS:<br /><br />&#34;The Tall Man&#34; begins as one type of thriller and quickly shifts gears into another type. It's rare that a director can pull of this slight-of-hand (The Prestige [Blu-ray], Stage Fright and Vertigo: Special Edition (Universal Legacy Series) are three that largely succeed at turning genres inside out)and, despite his ambition and talent, Pascal Laugier (Martyrs [Blu-ray]) doesn't have the skills to pull it off with &#34;The Tall Man&#34;; he can't pull the threads together to make this thriller either compelling. Laugier's glacial pacing does the film no favors either as the few moments of suspense that he is able to generate quickly dissipates leaving a thriller with no thrills. Laugier also does the film no favors by allowing the film to continue for 15 minutes after it should have ended. The points revealed could and should have been revealed in other ways (it could easily have been cross cut with the scene of the confession and would have worked better).<br /><br />That's too bad as the film is packed with strong supporting performances including well known faces from TV shows such as Stephen McHattie (Fringe: The Complete First Season), Sammantha Ferris (Supernatural: The Complete Fifth Season) and William B. Davis (The X-Files: The Complete First Season) doing a nice job. Even with the best performances from a supporting cast their roles are underwritten and Biel just doesn't have the depth as a performer to carry the film.<br /><br />&#34;The Tall Man&#34; looks decent if you keep in mind that the the intentional gloomy look of the film. The image doesn't have much depth.<br /><br />The audio sounds quite nice with a nice mix although if you listen in stereo you will find that the dialogue gets lost.<br /><br />As far as special features go we get a single deleted scene, the trailer and the Blu-ray has a compilation of conceptual artwork for the film.<br /><br />&#34;The Tall Man&#34; has ambition, an unusual concept and the director wants to turn the conventions of suspense thrillers on its head. Unfortunately, the devil is in the details (to use a cliche) and there's no devil truly here. Viewers have little tolerance for bait-and-switch movies (witness the mixed reaction to (The Cabin In The Woods [Blu-ray + UltraViolet Digital Copy]) and unless the director can skillfully pull off the project, it's not going to work. Unfortunately &#34;The Tall Man&#34; fails to live up to its potential.<br /><br />I would recommend arental first to see if this is to your taste based on the mixed reviews.rental first to see if this is to your taste based on the mixed reviews.

B005TKD512|3.0|The Heaths have written an accessible small book on change management.  It is based on three principles namely:<br />1. Make clear what needs to change and what must be done<br />2. Provide a strong case for wanting the change to take place and participating in the implementation of the change<br />3. Clear the path or situation for change since a people problem (resistance to change) is often a situational problem (unknown roadblocks, contradicting norms and bureaucratic rules etc.).<br /><br />These principles are useful as \\"quickies\\" especially if you are an internal or external consultant trying to convince your client to do something about an undesirable situation. The Heaths provide an example of how to win the minds of clients by getting the former to work out for themselves the real need to make the move to change.  The example based on the deficit model of management (as against the flourishing model) is compelling both to the client who it was meant to impress and to the reader (such as myself).  It is the kind of example an internal consultant may want to emulate.  The example has two characteristics:<br />(1) Within the context in which it was delivered by the internal consultant, the example of what was going on was sufficiently catastrophic to raise the emotions of the client<br />(2) It allowed the client to work out what it meant in terms of figures (instead of the internal consultant to work out the figures).  This provided the intellectual and cognitive motivation to pay attention to the evidence beyond figures.<br /><br />What is new: For people like me, who grew up on the OD masters of the 60 - 70s such as Beckhard and Harris, Schein, and so forth,there is nothing new. However the packaging of a well trodden message of what is required to create the motivation to change is worth a mark.<br /><br />Any weakness:  Yes, I thought that the Heaths run a danger of contradicting themselves when they use catchy but lasting messages such as \\"what looks like a people problem may be a situation problem\\" and then go on to say that \\"for every one to change someone has to act differently\\" thus  putting emphasis on people rather than situations.  This potential contradiction also appears in another appealing message namely: \\"People become exhausted trying to implement change\\" again returning to people rather than to situations.  Switch as a  \\"quickie\\" is worth reading and keeping for some time.  For teaching the fundamentals of change, I still find the OD masters a good starting point.ke a people problem may be a situation problem\\" and then go on to say that \\"for every one to change someone has to act differently\\" thus  putting emphasis on people rather than situations.  This potential contradiction also appears in another appealing message namely: \\"People become exhausted trying to implement change\\" again returning to people rather than to situations.  Switch as a  \\"quickie\\" is worth reading and keeping for some time.  For teaching the fundamentals of change, I still find the OD masters a good starting point.

B0071BGOJC|4.0|I simply love Ken Follet's historical fiction and this book was no exception, even though it took me a bit longer this time to get truly engaged into the story. Maybe it would have been easier if I had read Fall of Titans again directly before starting Winter of the World. The book has many different stories of people directly or indirectly connected with each other and it was a bit confusing in the beginning to connect the dots. However, what I appreciate is Mr. Follet's thorough research of historical events and that he never draws a black and white picture. He makes an effort to show what led to the events. For example he does not stigmatize the Japanese as being pure evil and imperialistic but points out that the American politicians had frozen their accounts and thus had cut them of the resources they needed for their economy. The Germans are also not all Nazis but there was quite some resistance. Mr. Follet never loses himself in stereotypes. His characters are complex and we understand why the nuclear physicist betrays his secrets to a communist spy, why the communist spy sticks with Stalin even though he hates what Stalin has done to the original communist idea and why the fervent and disillusioned young Nazi turns into a fervent communist at the end of the war. Besides being entertained I also learned a lot through this book. I am looking forward to part 3. Two thumbs up for Mr. Follet.

0887307280|5.0|The book revolves around a central idea, that there exists a myth (\\"E-Myth\\") which states: \\"Small businesses are started by entrepreneurs risking capital to make a profit. This is simply not so. The real reasons people start businesses have little to do with entrepreneurship. In fact, this belief in the Entrepreneurial Myth is the most important factor in the devastating rate of small business failure today. Understanding the E-Myth, and applying that understanding to creation and development of a small business, can be the secret to any business's success.\\"<br /><br />To overcome this myth and it's accompanying challenges, the author argues for the deployment of a Franchise Prototype model. It begins with the owner realizing that \\"your business is not your life...the primary purpose of your business is to serve your life, you can then go to work on your business, rather than in it\\".<br /><br />One might than ask themselves, how do I convert my existing business into this new operational model? This is where the Business Development Program, comes into play. The program introduced by GERBER in this book is based on the execution of the following seven steps:<br /><br />1- Your Primary Aim: \\" What do I value the most? What kind of life do I want? What do I want my life to look like, to feel like? Who do I wish to be? Your primary aim is the answer to all these questions.\\"<br /><br />2- Your Strategic Objective: \\"A very clear statement of what your business has to ultimately do for you to achieve your primary aim.\\"<br /><br />3- Your Organizational Strategy: Structure the way the business is going to work, in other words creating the organizational chart -  roles and responsibilities.<br /><br />4- Your Management Strategy: \\"A system designed into your prototype to produce a marketing result.\\"<br /><br />5- Your People Strategy: The way the \\"game\\" (vision/aim) is communicated to the team at the outset. This includes everything from the position contracts (organization chart), to operations manuals, to the standards for performance and accountability.<br /><br />6- Your Marketing Strategy: Knowing who your customer is (demographics) and why they buy (psychographics)<br /><br />7- Your Systems Strategy: The \\"set of things, actions, ideas and information that interact with each other, and in so doing, alter other systems.\\"<br /><br />What sets this book apart is the analysis that the author performs, through a sample business, of issues small business owners encounter. This includes the different personas the owner takes on, as well as the evolution of the business through the maturity cycle. This analysis is what allows the readers to appreciate and embrace the proposed prototype framework that the author then introduces as key to success. A must read in the area of entrepreneurship and small business.chart), to operations manuals, to the standards for performance and accountability.<br /><br />6- Your Marketing Strategy: Knowing who your customer is (demographics) and why they buy (psychographics)<br /><br />7- Your Systems Strategy: The \\"set of things, actions, ideas and information that interact with each other, and in so doing, alter other systems.\\"<br /><br />What sets this book apart is the analysis that the author performs, through a sample business, of issues small business owners encounter. This includes the different personas the owner takes on, as well as the evolution of the business through the maturity cycle. B008GX2YQQ|4.0|So far every Animal Collective album to date has been radically different the the last while at the same time introducing the listener to combinations of styles from all over music history and the world, which is one of my favorite qualities of any band. Not only this but the songwriting and emotion delivered on every album has been powerful and heartfelt, from Avey Tare's wordy Sid Barret style lyrics to Panda Bear's mantra meets nursery-rhyme approach.  This album, to me, represents one the few territories Animal Collective had yet to try out:  The traditional rock band approach.  Replacing Merriweather's looped electronic beats and minimal percussion Panda Bear is sitting down at a drum kit for the first time since the band's very early days, albeit sans snare drum and high hat (snare being replaced by two congas and giant shaker filling the usual space of the high hat).  Also new to the soundscape are actual bass lines where previously there had only been minimal bass or none at all.  The songwriting has also taken a turn for the more direct.  Animal Collective are known for throwing out the rule book on traditional verse-chorus-verse structure but on Centipede Hz most songs have a very recognizable verse-bridge-chorus pop/rock song structure which actually leads to some pretty dense songs that can only be fully grasped upon repeated listens.<br />Many have complained that the band isn't doing anything new on Centipede Hz and while that may be true in the scope of music history I would say that they are certainly doing something new for themselves.  All in all the songwriting is strong, with one or two exceptions.  Avey has once again taken most of the songwriting duties with Panda only including two songs (both great in my opinion) and Deakin finally contributing a song of his own that is a little long winded but has a great finish and is a perfect middle-point to the album.  In the context of Animal Collective records I don't think this is the best they have made, but I still think it's a great album from one of the most influential groups of the last decade.

B008C1O8CA|3.0|Billie Joe Armstrong said, \\"We are at the most prolific and creative time in our lives.\\"  Prolific?  Sure.  This album is the first of a trilogy so there was clearly a lot of material in the works.  Creative?  I don't know.  Maybe we'll hear some of that on the two upcoming releases.  Their best decision was to not attempt another remake of \\"American Idiot\\" like they did with \\"21st Century Breakdown.\\"  While that album had many fine moments, the over-the-top production mixed with the bombastic nature of some of the songs made it seem a bit too obvious that the guys were copying themselves.  Between the two releases was the Foxboro Hot Tubs side project, which seems to be more of who Green Day truly is.  It made \\"21st Century\\" seem insincere and unnecessarily polished in their quest for a repeat success of the \\"American Idiot\\" phenomenon.  Even Billie Joe has called \\"Dos,\\" the upcoming second release in the trilogy, \\"the second Foxboro album.\\"<br /><br />So what do we have with \\"Uno\\"?  It's always hard to follow complex productions with a more stripped down sound and appear like you're giving it your all.  That's how albums like Weezer's Green Album or Sloan's \\"Action Pact\\" come about. Even go back to the Beatles' \\"White Album.\\"  A band can either keep pushing forward, or retreat and go \\"back to their roots\\" when things become hard to top/follow.  What \\"Uno\\" seems to consist of are very catchy songs that all sound the same.  Production-wise, there is nothing interesting on this album whatsoever.  It starts off with a solid 1-2-3-4 punch before \\"Kill the DJ\\" hits us, which may be the worst song ever to appear on a Green Day album.  I'm surprised a song with nearly 20 f-bombs was released as a single, but that may have been an attempt to make people believe there is more diversity to this album than there actually is.  That, and the throwaway \\"Troublemaker,\\" are the low points of the album.<br /><br />While some of the tunes aren't very memorable, it's still a fun andcatchy set of harmless songs.  But repeat listens won't be rewarded with any new insights.  I happened to find \\"AI\\" and \\"21st\\" more melodic and interesting musically.  I reject all the comparisons to \\"Warning\\" that I'm reading about.  \\"Warning\\" took chances in style and instrumentation with harmonica, mandolin, accordion, strings, and more.  If anything this is \\"Insomniac II,\\" just not as good.  \\"Insomniac\\" was a 32-minute onslaught of energy with only \\"Brain Stew\\" to break up the pace.  All those songs sound similar but you don't mind, or even notice, because it was their fourth album (second to many people) and we didn't know at the time all they would be capable of in the years ahead.  Two songs here: \\"Fell For You\\" and \\"Sweet 16\\" sound like they could have been on either \\"39/Smooth\\" or \\"Kerplunk,\\" but \\"Uno\\" is not a return to those days like so many would have you believe.<br /><br />The album is fun, but not as fun as Foxboro.  On that release, Green Day were laid back, enjoying themselves, and letting it all hang out.  This album is carrying the Green Day name which, like \\"21st Century Breakdown,\\" the guys won't allow to appear on a release that is anything less than radio-friendly, polished, and an instant invite to be next to Foo Fighters as the only rock bands allowed to appear at award shows anymore.  The songs on \\"AI\\" and \\"21st\\" have multiple parts, bridges, and seemingly unrelated sections, which add up to an entertaining listen even with the albums as long as they are.  Like I said, when you are going to strip things down and do a straight-forward rock album like this, it can still be a blast, but it also appears like you're phoning it in.  We'll see what they're saving for \\"Dos\\" and \\"Tre.\\"

B007MB5OCE|4.0|This was a fun read, even though it tended to get a bit silly, making fun of world events and leaders.  After a bit, I came to understand that the author's style was fully intending to be sarcastic, as well as inane.  So I just kept on reading, being fully entertained and laughing out loud.  The writer capitalizes on his career as a journalist and researcher to bring to the reader a series of ironic and tongue-in-cheek events, in a rather loosely built plot.  But that is purely the author's intent.  Trying to read more into the plot or characters is nonsense and would spoil the sheer pleasure of this clever persiflage.<br /><br />The premise for the tale is that a very elderly, widely traveled Swede decides to ditch his 100th birthday, at old folks home.  Hence he escapes back in the big, wide world, from which he had made so many interesting friends and captured many unique experiences.  Could one fault him for such a spur-of-the-moment decision?  Not I!<br /><br />Through a series of ten decades, in which the main character accidentally runs into fame and notoriety, the maturing man learns that life is truly full of ups and downs.  The plot is thick with clever irony and tongue-in-cheek comments about the machinations of world politics.  In all of this, the author has created a man who takes all life events in stride, taking the good with the bad, having a positive approach to life and becoming the quintessential carpe diem sort of guy.  Thus, after failing to show up for his 100th birthday bash at the rest home, the author invents a series of well-placed mishaps, flashbacks, crazy characters and mad escapes and to bring the centenarian \\"home\\" to continue to mix and mingle with a madcap group of fellow existentialists.<br /><br />If you're looking for great literature, this is not your kind of read. If you need a good, long-winded laugh to brighten your day, do go for this tale.  The author makes no apologies about his intent to entertain, except for the fact thatone has to wonder if all the world's major events aren't just results of accidentally placed people and their circumstance.  Hmmmmm.....

B008O037RG|2.0|Millions of people adore Mumford & Sons, finding their sound to be much more than pleasant folksy tunes but rather something like a revelatory, deeply meaningful expression of passion.<br /><br />When I first heard M&S, I, too, found them revelatory. It was intensely refreshing to hear popular music that has soul--so much soul that they couldn't help but to project it at the tops of their lungs. It was a desperately needed reply to the current \\"I don't care / we do what we want\\" irreverent dance-pop glitz ethos.<br /><br />Many listens later, I see M&S differently. The music reliably invokes excitement but, in doing so, it finds no space for subtlety or understatement. Their roots are in Back Country bluegrass and folk -- genres that are all about stories -- but in M&S's music there are no stories. Rather, this album is a lot like U2's City of Blinding Light: Biblical imagery expressed in generic terms. A flailing attempt to capture spirituality. Or maybe just to prevent boredom. Instead of stories intended to shake and inspire, we get posturing and shouting intended to excite. After a while, all the excitement becomes exhausting and empty, not unlike the dance-pop glitz they oppose.<br /><br />I believe people are starved for deeper rewards than Maroon 5 and their dance-pop contemporaries offer, and I believe that's why M&S are the top-selling musicians in the country (and by a wide margin), because they give the instant impression of heartfelt folky soulfulness. But the truth, revealed after enough listens, is that they are closer to stadium rock. To find deeper rewards, you have to look to the folk / bluegrass / celtic roots that have inspired them: Bob Dylan or Van Morrison, or even more recent acts like Ray LaMontagne or Amos Lee. Their music may not be as instantly pleasurable or exciting as M&S's, but if you give it your patience and attention, you just might find rewards that are far more precious than excitement.

In the first section Amy's chapters start out as diary entries that begin back before they were married and continue up to her disappearance.<br /><br />In this psychological thriller, the writing is stunning, clever, subtle, witty, and chillingly suspenseful. 1439102430|3.0|If you are a fan of the FOX television series \\"Bones\\" and you pick up one of Kathy Reichs' Temperance Brennan novels you will be in for a rude awakening.  To begin, with the exception of Temperance hardly any of the characters from the TV series are featured in the novels and her on-air love interest --- Booth --- is a composite of two characters in the novels (Andrew Ryan and Ollie Hasty).<br /><br />The latest Brennan novel, BONES ARE FOREVER, is the fifteenth in this successful series that provided inspiration for the hit show. Even though this novel begins with a forensic mystery it soon takes a sharp twist and the end result is a story unlike all those prior in this series.<br />A woman using the name Amy Roberts checks into a Montreal hospital with a case of uncontrolled bleeding and promptly disappears.  When Temperance Brennan and her crime-fighting partner, Detective Andrew Ryan are dispatched to follow the case they turn up a truly grisly find.  Upon arrival at Mr. Roberts' address they find the badly decomposed bodies of three infants and Roberts is nowhere to be found.<br /><br />Making matters more complicated is that no one knows for sure who the real Amy Roberts is.  Her landlord has her listed as Alma Rogers and a recent boyfriend swears she is Alva Rodriguez.  The trail soon stretches across Canada to Edmonton and forces Tempe and Ryan to call on the resources of Royal Canadian Mounted Police Sergeant Ollie Hasty.  This introduction also makes for interesting reading as Ollie and Temperance have a brief fling in their past and this causes obvious tension with the newly formed trio.<br /><br />As the hunt into the mysterious Ms. Roberts past gets deeper the novel takes its' sharp turn.  BONES ARE FOREVER moves far away from a standard forensic mystery and instead digs deep into the sordid underworld of Edmonton and the Northwest territories.  Specifically, an illegal diamond-smuggling and mining ring appears to be at the bottom of the Amy Roberts mystery and places Temperance and company in the cross-hairs of some highly dangerous individuals.<br />As opposed to other Brennan novels which jump between locations, particularly Canada and North Carolina, BONES ARE FOREVER stays situated in Canada and provides some eye-opening peeks into what is assumed to be a peaceful and tranquil country.  Kathy Reichs herself indicates that it was her personal role in some child homicide cases that created the impetus for this novel.  She also became quite interested in diamond-mining controversy in certain parts of Canada and cleverly combined the two story-lines into one plot.<br /><br />I was somewhat disappointed at how easily the `Amy Roberts' story-line is wrapped up and quickly supplanted by the diamond-mining plotline but also recognize that to keep a long-running series going you need to step out of character occasionally and take chances.  While not a traditional `bones' story, BONES ARE FOREVER raises some clear moral issues that Kathy Reichs obviously feels strongly about and their impacts resonate through all her characters.<br /><br />Reviewed by Ray Palen for New Mystery Reader

I've liked all of their previous albums, and I like how they experiment, weaving in all sorts of genres and styles and embossing them with a giant bombastic MUSE stamp of musicality. Their yearly reinvention is part of the fun! However, the songs on this album seem safe, derivative, and just a little bit tired, as if Matt Bellamy needs a nice long nap.<br /><br />This is not an album, just a collection of songs. There's no cohesive thread running through the mix -- the CD starts strong and gradually winnows away into forgettable songs. Occasional sparks of genius are overshadowed by simple, safe arrangements, or weaker repetitions of stuff they've already done better on old albums.<br /><br />The inclusion of their Olympic song (\\"Survival\\") seems completely out of place with the rest of the album. The Wolstenholme songs are good enough, but they're not MUSE at all (maybe a solo album would have been better?). \\"Save Me\\" sounds like Muse trying to be Coldplay, and \\"Liquid State\\" sounds like Finger Eleven trying to be Muse. The CD ends with another mini-symphony (\\"2nd Law\\"), and it's more soundtrack than rock song. I didn't mind the dubstep bits but it felt over the top and not in a good \\"Knights of Cydonia\\" way (more like a \\"Ross Gellar plays the keyboards\\" way).<br /><br />I'm disappointed that this album was just good and not great. As \\"MUSE's next big album\\" it's a meandering mess. Had it been advertised as a collection of B-sides instead, it wouldn't be half bad. If you're a diehard fan, you've probably already bought this album. If you just want a couple great tunes to blast in the car, try a couple of the MP3s instead.
